English

When a desired object is incapable of attainment by oneself and by other up─Бyas,
prapatti is the placing of the responsibility or burden of securing it in somebody who is capable of doing so
with a request or supplication.
It is declared to be the specific thought such as (the following):

“This object should be accomplished (for me) by you
without my making any effort of my own hereafter.”

English

In this up─Бya ( consisting of angi and aс╣Еgas ) to be adopted by the seeker after mokс╣гa ,
the ang─л is the surrender of one’s self or ─Бtm─Б
with a clear understanding (that)
neither in the prapatti nor in the fruit thereof, one has any independence;
it should be in the same way as one would surrender a jewel belonging to another
to that person himself
to be kept safe by him
and to be worn by him.

That is; one should realise that,
in relation to the Lord of all who appears in the base and the suffix of the first letter in the praс╣Зava (i.e. “a” which means I┼Ыvara and the suffix of the dative or fourth case which has been dropped i.e. aya (for the Lord of all))
as the protector of all and the ┼Ыeс╣г─л of all,
one has no interest or connection at all
in the activity of protecting one-self or those related to one-self
and also in what results from the protection of oneself and those related to oneself,
either as depending upon one self
or as bringing about some results for oneself.
It is the specific form of thought
that one is ┼Ыeс╣гa to the Lord
and is entirely dependent upon the Lord -
in this, the most important feature is
surrendering the responsibility of protection (bharany─Бsa) to the Lord.

рдЗрдиреНрдж рд╢реЗрд╖рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрд╕рдиреНрдзрд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддреНрддреИ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард┐рдХреНрдХреБрдореН рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рддреНрддреИрдХреН рдХрд╛рдЯреНрдЯреБрдЧрд┐рд▒рд╛рд░реН рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рдордпрд┐ рдирд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреЗрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ ред рдЗрдиреНрдж рд╡рдЪрдирдореН рднрдЧрд╡рд╛рдйрд┐рдбрддреНрддрд┐рд▓реН рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рд╡рд┐рдйреБрдбреИрдп рдирд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрддреНрддреИ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдХреНрдХрд┐рд▒рджреБред рдОрдйреНрд▒реБ рдЪреЛрджрд┐рддрдорд╛рдй - рдЗрд╡реНрд╡рдЪрдирддреНрддрд┐рд▓реН рд╕реКрдйреНрдйрдмрдбрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдорд╛рдй, рдЗрд╡реНрд╡рдиреБрд╕рдиреНрдзрд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддреНрдд - рдлрд▓рднрд░рдиреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдЧрд░реНрднрдорд╛рдй рдХреАрд┤реНрдЪреНрдЪреКрдйреНрдй рд╢реЗрд╖рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрд╕рдиреНрдзрд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддреНрддреИ, рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард┐рдХреНрдХреБрдореНрдмрдбрд┐ - рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард┐рдХреНрдХреБрдореН рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рдореНред рдЗрджрд▒реНрдХреБ рднрд╛рд╡рд┐рдХреНрдХреИ рдпреЖрдйреНрдмрджреЛрдбрдиреНрд╡рдпрдореНред

The person should realise this within himself: viz.,

“I am absolutely dependent (upon the Lord);

and has no dependence on anybody else.

and who is independent
should protect me for the fulfilment of His own purposes.

English

As is said in the ┼Ыloka :

“Even myself or ─Бtm─Б does not belong to me;
(if a man should consider what does not belong to him as his,
he could consider the whole earth as his )';

my soul does not belong to me,
it does not belong to anyone else (than Bhagav─Бn),
I do not belong to myself,

nor can I say that any thing belongs to me unconditionally.

To all seekers of mokс╣гa (whether bhaktas or prapannas),
the surrender of one’s svar┼лpa or self and the rest (i.e) the fruit in common.

the surrender of the responsibility of protection (bharany├бsa ) is an additional aс╣Еg─л.

рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдГ (рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯреБрдВ рдиреЛрджреНрдпрдореН)

рддреНрдпрдХреНрдд-рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛-рдлрд▓-рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореНрдпрдВ
рд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдо-рд╕рдорд░реНрдкрдгрдореН рее реирео-рдЗрее

English

─Бtmasamarpanam (the surrendering of the self to the Lord for protection) means here
the realisation of the self as existing solely for the purpose of the Saviour
and that to such an extent that the self feels no further responsibility, whatever, for its own protection
and this should be accompanied by the knowledge that the fruits of such surrender are not one’s own.

рдХреГрдд-рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮреЛ рднреВрд╖рдг-рдиреАрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХреЗрдирдЪрд┐рджреН +рдзреЗрддреБрдирд╛ рд╕реНрд╡-рд╣рд╕реНрддрдЧрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдореН,

English

If a man has (somehow) come into possession of a cloth bag with the king’s seal on it,
he would return the bag (to the king),
even though he does not know for certain the nature and character of the gem contained within it,
in the hope that the king would take it back.

рддрд╛рд╡рдиреН-рдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдгрд╛рдкрд┐ рдЕрдирд╛рджрд┐-рдХрд╛рд▓-рдХреГрддрд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдкрд╣рд╛рд░-рдЪреМрд░реНрдп-рдЬрдирд┐рддреЛ рднрдЧрд╡рдиреН-рдирд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдГ рд╢рд╛рдореНрдпреЗрджреН
рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рддрд╛рддреНрдкрд░реНрдпрдореН ред

English

So also even those who have not the intelligence to know, with perfect clearness,
the nature, character and state of the soul as distinguished from the body
may surrender their self or soul with the little knowledge that they possess.
If they do so,
even for that much,
Bhagav─Бn will be prepared to remit the punishment for the theft
consisting in making away with one’s self (i. e. claiming it as one’s own) from beginningless time.

This idea contained in the ┼Ы─Бstras is what (Aс╕╖avand─Бr) has in mind.

This idea contained in the ┼Ы─Бstras is what (Aс╕╖avand─Бr) has in mind.

рдПрддрджреН рдЕрдЧреНрд░реЗ, тАЬ9 рдордо рдирд╛рде рдпрджрд╕реНрддрд┐” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХреЗ

рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдкрд╣рд╛рд░-рдЪреМрд░реНрдпрдореН рдЙрдиреНрдореВрд▓рд┐рддрдВ рди рднрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрдЬреН-рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред

English

In the next *┼Ыloka (53)1 it might appear as if he revoked the surrender (made before);
but its meaning is only this :
Even when a person is bent on surrendering his self
without a knowledge of such things as the nature of his self,
if he surrenders it with the notion that it is his own,
like the presentation to a king of something belonging to oneself,
it would not completely put an end to the crime of having stolen one’s self.

Espa├▒ol

In the next *┼Ыloka (53)2 it might appear as if he revoked the surrender (made before);
but its meaning is only this :
Even when a person is bent on surrendering his self
without a knowledge of such things as the nature of his self,
if he surrenders it with the notion that it is his own,
like the presentation to a king of something belonging to oneself,
it would not completely put an end to the crime of having stolen one’s self.

English

So from these two ┼Ыloka s,
it is clear that the essence of the ┼Ы─Бstras
which primarily prescribe bharasamarpaс╣Зam as in the words of Aс╕╖avand─Бr (60)

“The responsibility of protecting me is also Thine”,

consists in saying “na mama” = тАЬIt is not mine”
and getting rid of the feeling of one’s connection (with everything),
though one may not have a true and discriminatory knowledge
about such things as the essential nature of the self.

English

Thus in the first part of the Dvaya which deals with the up─Бya or means,
the surrender to the Lord of the responsibility (for one’s protection)
accompanied by the thought that one is ┼Ыeс╣гa to the Lord
and exists only for Him
is to be understood in connection with the verb (prapadye)
joined with the word ┼Ыaranam
which treats of the up─Бya preceded by supreme faith ( mahavisv─Бsa )
and which contains within it, in an implicit form, the supplication for protection.

and which contains within it, in an implicit form, the supplication for protection.

English

Thus (from what has been said in this chapter and in the foregoing chapters),
although these six (the five aс╣Еgas and the ang─л) may be understood separately,
while considering, in detail, the meaning of each part of the sentence,
yet they constitute only a single mental act
while understanding the whole sentence,
just like the understanding of other sentences having several parts.

English

An archer’s action in discharging an arrow for hitting a target
may be constituted of several separate acts
(like observing the object,
taking the aim
and discharging the arrow) and yet it is all accomplished in a single moment.
Similar is the act of surrendering (to the Lord) the responsibility of (one’s) protection.
This is evident from the ┼Ыruti itself.

(The ┼Ыruti says,
“* Praс╣Зava (aum) is the bow:
the soul or self is the arrow;
it must be discharged at Brahman, which is the target,
with great care and with keen concentration “).

рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдГ (рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯреБрдВ рдиреЛрджреНрдпрдореН)

рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирддрдпрд╛ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рддрд╛рд╡рддреН -
рдХрд░реНрддреБрддреНрд╡-рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ–рдордорддрд╛-рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ– рдлрд▓-рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ–рдлрд▓реЛрдкрд╛рдпрддреНрд╡-рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧ-рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХрдВ
рдЖрдиреБрдХреВрд▓реНрдп-рд╕рдВрдХрд▓реНрдкрд╛рджреНрдпреН-рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рдиреБрд╕рдиреНрдзрд╛рдиреЗрди рд╕рд╣
рдЧреБрд░реБ-рдкрд░рдореНрдкрд░реЛрдкрд╕рддреНрддрд┐-рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ–рджреНрд╡рдп-рд╡рдЪрди-рдореБрдЦреЗрди

English

In (the performance of) this (ang─л),
the conclusion regarding the adoption of this up─Бya with its aс╣Еgas
is as follows:-
it consists in the act of surrendering
the responsibility for the protection of one’s self
preceded by the following:–

  • the giving up of the thought that one is the doer
    (for it is the Lord that does everything),
  • the giving up of the thought of ‘mine’
    (that there is anything belonging to oneself),
  • the giving up of the fruit of the action,
  • the giving up of the thought
    that he himself adopts the means for obtaining that fruit;

these must be accompanied by anuk┼лlya saс╣Еkalpa, pratikulyavarjana and the rest and, likewise, reverent bowing down to the succession of gurus and with the utterance of Dvaya.

The surrender of the responsibility for the protection of one’s self
carries with it implicitly the surrender of one’s Svar┼лpa or self
and the fruit or gain arising from it.

English

The giving up of the thought that one is the doer
will result from the realisation of one’s entire dependance on the Lord
throughout the existence of the soul.

This will make one know that
this doership has been vouchsafed to one by the Lord Himself.

English

The giving up of the thought of ‘MINE’ (mama) and of the fruit (of prapatti)
will arise from the knowledge that one,
as well as what belongs to one,
exists, by one’s very nature,
solely for the fulfilment of the purposes of Bhagav─Бn alone.

surgir├б del conocimiento de que uno,
as├н como lo que pertenece a uno,
existe, por la misma naturaleza,
├║nicamente para el cumplimiento de los prop├│sitos de Bhagav─Бn solo.

English

The giving up of the up─Бya for attaining the fruit (mokс╣гa )
will result from a knowledge that
the prapatti performed by a man for winning the grace of the Saviour

  • cannot directly and immediately be the cause of the main fruit, namely, mokс╣гa ,
  • that prapatti is non-sentient and, therefore, incapable of possessing the will to grant the fruit

and that only I┼Ыvara is the up─Бya for this fruit (mokс╣гa ).

English
  • Since Bhagav─Бn who, out of the love natural to Him, has been the primaeval cause of everything
    from the time of giving the man the body and the senses
    to the time of his uttering the Dvaya-
  • since Bhagav─Бn is possessed of the will
    accompanied by the desire to show His grace
    and is the immediate and direct cause (of the final fruit, viz. mokс╣гa )
  • and since he also stands Himself in the place of the prescribed up─Бya
    in the case of the man who is incapable of (adopting) other up─Бyas,

He alone is the up─Бya for the fruit.

рдПрд╡рдВрднрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдп рдореВрд▓рдВ
рдзрд░реНрдорд┐-рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдХ-рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ-рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдЗрддрд┐,
рдЕрдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдереЛ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реН рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддреБрдВ рди рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ ред

English

The authority for this conclusion is the nature of the object, (namely, Bhagav─Бn)
as understood from the ┼Ы─Бstra
which reveals the Person who has that nature;
and this authority cannot be challenged by reason.

Espa├▒ol

La autoridad para esta conclusi├│n es la naturaleza del objeto (a saber, bhagav─Бn)
como se entiende de la ┼Ъ─Бstra
lo que revela a la persona que tiene esa naturaleza;
y esta autoridad no puede ser cuestionada por la raz├│n.

hacer lo que es agradable
y abstinencia de lo que es desagradable

como accesorios o aс╣Еgas para el up─Бya.

we take the avoidance of what is displeasing as meaning only the determination to avoid what is displeasing,

тАЬ12 рдЕрдкрд╛рдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛ рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐” рдЗрддреНрдпреН-рдЙрдХреНрдд-рд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╜рднрд┐рд╕рдиреНрдзрд┐-рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдо-рд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡реЗрд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд╛
рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд┐рдХреВрд▓реНрдп-рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк-рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐-рд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд╛

рдкрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдлрд▓рдВ рднрд╡рд┐рддреБрдореН рдЕрд░реНрд╣рддрд┐ ред

English

It is true that it has been said :-
“I have dissociated myself from sins which cast one into saс╣Бs─Бra.”
(But it may be explained in this way :-)
The avoidance of what is displeasing may mean
either having no connection (at all) with it (i.e.) giving it up
or the determination to avoid it.
In either case, this is, at the first instant, an aс╣Еga
and the actual avoidance is the result or fruit of prapatti which follows afterwards.

Espa├▒ol

Es cierto que se ha dicho:-
“Me he disociado de los pecados que arrojan uno a Saс╣Бs─Бra”.
(Pero puede explicarse de esta manera :-)
La evitaci├│n de lo que es desagradable puede significar

  • o no tener conexi├│n (en absoluto) con ella - (es decir), renunciando a
  • o la determinaci├│n de evitarlo.

En cualquier caso, este es, en el primer instante, un Aс╣ЕGA
y la evitaci├│n real es el resultado o fruto de Prapatti que sigue despu├йs.

рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓реЗрд╖реБ
рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд╢реН рдЪрд╛рдиреНрдпрддрдГ рдлрд▓рдореН ред
рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдмреНрдз-рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН
рд╕рдЩреНрдХрд▓реНрдкреЗ +++(рд╕рддрд┐)+++ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рдкрддреНрддрд┐рддрдГ рее реирео-рдЕ рее

English

Doing what is pleasing (to the Lord)
and avoiding what is displeasing (in one’s life after prapatti)
are the result of meritorious deeds done in the past,
and also the determination made at the time of performing prapatti.

Espa├▒ol

Haciendo lo que es agradable (para el Se├▒or)
y evitando lo que es desagradable (en la vida de uno despu├йs de Prapatti)
son el resultado de acciones meritorias realizadas en el pasado,
y tambi├йn la determinaci├│n realizada en el momento de realizar Prapatti.

English

Therefore wise are they who perform prapatti
in order to render faultless service during their life-time
and to attain mokс╣гa after casting off the body resulting from pr─Бrabdha karma.

Espa├▒ol

Por lo tanto, sabios son los que realizan Prapatti
Para prestar un servicio impecable durante su vida ├║til
y para alcanzar Mokс╣гa despu├йs de expulsar el cuerpo como resultado de Pr─Бrabdha Karma.

рдЗрддрд┐ (рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдп ) рее

English

Our princely ─Бc─Бrya s, who wear the crown of proficiency in the Vedas,
have placed us for protection under the feet of the Lord,
who, from beginningless time, has resolved, in His great compassion, to save us;
they have done so in order that there may be no further responsibility in ourselves (for our protection),
by saying to us,

“Do not forget the truth that the Lord,
who is the soul of the world,
will protect you who are related to Him as ┼Ыeс╣гa (existing solely for His purposes),”

Espa├▒ol

Nuestros principescos ─Бc─Бrya s, que usan la corona de la competencia en los Vedas,
nos han colocado para protecci├│n bajo los pies del Se├▒or,
quien, desde el tiempo sin inicio, ha resuelto, en su gran compasi├│n, de salvar nos;
Lo han hecho para que no haya m├бs responsabilidad en nosotros mismos (para nuestra protecci├│n),
dici├йndonos,

“No olvides la verdad que el Se├▒or,
Quien es el alma del mundo
te proteger├б que est├йn relacionados con ├йl como ┼Ъeс╣гa (existente ├║nicamente para sus prop├│sitos) “.

English

The horse, the chariot and the charioteer –
the end of the Vedas (the Upaniс╣гads) shows that the three tattvas, cit, acit, and I┼Ыvara are related to one another respectively like the three mentioned above
and have always had varied activities
in accordance with their respective nature.

In connection with these activities,
all the three are of the nature of being the (material) causes;
two, cit and I┼Ыvara, are of the nature of doers,
and one (1.) I┼Ыvara is alone independent (of all others).

Therefore the j─лva,
the responsibility for whose protection has been undertaken by I┼Ыvara who is the Master, is carefree
and has no further responsibility of his own in the matter of his protection.

El caballo, el carro y el auriga - El final de los Vedas (los Upaniс╣гads) muestra que los tres tattvas, CIT, ACIT e I┼Ыvara est├бn relacionados entre s├н, respectivamente, como los tres mencionados anteriormente.
y siempre han tenido actividades variadas
de acuerdo con su naturaleza respectiva.

En relaci├│n con estas actividades,
Los tres son de la naturaleza de ser las causas (materiales);
Dos, Cit e I┼Ыvara, son de la naturaleza de los hacedores,
y uno (1.) I┼Ыvara es solo independiente (de todos los dem├бs).

Por lo tanto, el J─лva,
La responsabilidad de cuya protecci├│n ha sido emprendida por I┼Ыvara, que es el maestro, es despreocupado
y no tiene m├бs responsabilidad propia
en el asunto de su protecci├│n.

рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджрд╣реЛрдмрд┐рд▓рдордард╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдкрдЯреНрдЯреЗ рдореВрд░реНрджреНрдзрд╛рднрд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрд╕реНрдп рдирд┐рд░рд╡рдзрд┐рдХрдЧреБрд░реБрднрдХреНрддрд┐рднрд░рд┐рддрд╕реНрдп рд╢реНрд░реАрд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореАрдиреГрд╕рд┐рдВрд╣рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдкрд╛рджреБрдХрд╛рд╕реЗрд╡рдХ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╡рдгреНрд╢рдардХреЛрдк рд╢реНрд░реА рд╢реНрд░реАрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд╢рдардХреЛрдкрдпрддреАрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХреГрддреМ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рд░рдмреЛрдзрд┐рдиреНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдкреНрд░рдкрджрдирд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░реЛ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рдГ рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдХрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд░реНрдХрд┐рдХрд╕рд┐рдВрд╣рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рддрдиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп

рд╢реНрд░реАрдорддреЗ рдирд┐рдЧрдорд╛рдиреНрддрдорд╣рд╛рджреЗрд╢рд┐рдХрд╛рдп рдирдордГ рее

  1. тАЬрдордо рдирд╛рде рдпрджрд╕реНрддрд┐ рдпреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдореНрдпрд╣рдВ рд╕рдХрд▓рдВ рддрджреНрдзрд┐ рддрд╡реИрд╡ рдорд╛рдзрд╡ ред рдирд┐рдпрддрд╕реНрд╡рдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдмреБрджреНрдзрдзреАрд░рдерд╡рд╛ рдХрд┐рдиреНрдиреБ рд╕рдорд░реНрдкрдпрд╛рдорд┐ рддреЗрее рдЖрд│рд╡рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реН рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдореН-релрей

    However O lord, what can I surrender to Thee, O Madhava,
    when I know that I and whatever belongs to me are always thine.
    As I have nothing of my own, I have nothing to surrender,
    I am only giving Thee what belongs to Thee”, ↩︎

  2. тАЬрдордо рдирд╛рде рдпрджрд╕реНрддрд┐ рдпреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдореНрдпрд╣рдВ рд╕рдХрд▓рдВ рддрджреНрдзрд┐ рддрд╡реИрд╡ рдорд╛рдзрд╡ ред рдирд┐рдпрддрд╕реНрд╡рдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдмреБрджреНрдзрдзреАрд░рдерд╡рд╛ рдХрд┐рдиреНрдиреБ рд╕рдорд░реНрдкрдпрд╛рдорд┐ рддреЗрее рдЖрд│рд╡рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реН рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдореН-релрей

    However O lord, what can I surrender to Thee, O Madhava,
    when I know that I and whatever belongs to me are always thine.
    As I have nothing of my own, I have nothing to surrender,
    I am only giving Thee what belongs to Thee”, ↩︎
